I made this twice, first as written and it was GREAT!  But then I did some mild modifications.  I used all ground beef, addes red wine instead of water and added 1/2 tsp of oregano and rosemary plus 2 bay leaves.  Put it in my crock pot for 4 hours and it was OUTSTANDING!  I even had a true Italian guy tell me it was an outstanding sauce.  I served it over spaghetti.

text:
I made this just for kicks to see how other people make their sauce. This was just OK at best. First of all...there's already enough fennel seed in Italian sausage that adding more is complete overkill. And it's definitely lacking ingredients for a full, rich sauce...such as...bell pepper, mushrooms, fresh Italian basil, fresh spicy oregano, fresh parsley, and a bit of red wine. (by the way...red wine is what should be used instead of sugar) Also...1/8 to 1/4 cup olive oil in your sauce will keep it from coagulating and also makes it a healthier recipe. A couple pinches of black pepper and fresh thyme sprinkled on the sauce when served finishes it off.

text:
Awesome meat sauce!!!  I sauteed the beef and sausage separately as they tend to be greasy and added them to the sauce during the last half hour of cooking.  I then sauteed the onion with a little olive oil and garlic until translucent.  I then added the tomatoes and spices.  I used red wine vs. water, added 1/4 tsp. of red pepper flakes, doubled the basil, added 2 tsp. of oregano, and 1 bay leaf.  The fennel seeds are a nice touch!  This sauce was so good and tasted even better the next day.

text:
I have been making this recipe for a long time now.  It is excellent.  Over time I made a few changes that perfect this recipe!  1)  Add more garlic!  You really can't put in too much!  2)  Substitute a dry red wine for half of the the water.  3)  Add 4-6 chopped fresh basil leaves!  You'll love the aroma in the kitchen, and be amazed at how it affects the taste of the sauce.  4)  Add about 1/2 tsp of oregano, and 1 bay leaf.  Amazing pasta sauce!

We took this to a pasta potluck and received many compliments and requests for the recipe! My daughter actually made it and said it was quick and easy. [But not quite as good as her husband's ;-)] Since everyone seemed to really like it I rated it five stars.  Personally, it was too much meat for me and next time I will cut the sugar in half or omit it entirely.  If you can find the Contadina brand tomato products I recommend using them.  Their flavor is less acidic than other brands.  This may be why I didn't think it needed the sugar.  Their roasted garlic flavored tomato paste is the best!!

text:
I live in Brussels and my husband is Italian. His grandmother lived in Dabruzzo in Italy and he always raved about her pasta sauce, until she died last year. So, I made this pasta sauce for him and he was mortified by how sweet it was. 2 tablespoons of sugar in a pasta sauce is apparently just not done. It is an American perversion of things done up like ketchup. The sugar just blew the thing to shreds. If I make this again, I'm going to change everything using the recommendations of folks on here, but more likely I'll try to find a recipe in a local cookbook.

text:
I have to admit this is a very, very good meat sauce. With the exception of adding fennel (store was out or didn't carry it) I followed the recipe until the end of the cooking time. BTW I worked and was taught at a very large Italian restaurant in Massachusetts so I think I have a decent tongue. When all was done I tasted it. Good...very good, yet with no uniqueness or direction. I added a bit of salt and that helped, but it took a half cup of cabernet to really make the other flavors pop out. Five minutes extra uncovered with some stirring to mix it in. Served over spaghetti with a Zinfandel on the side made a great meal.
We all have different tastes and this sauce could have turned in a different direction by using a 1/4 cup of bourbon instead of the wine.
I like the addition of the mild or sweet sausage and I suppose one could spend a lifetime trying all the varieties of those in your sauce. Ah...What a pleasure it will be.

text:
Oh my goodness - fixed pretty much as recipe called for - delicious.  Only addition was some homemade meatballs I had in the freezer that needed to be used up so skipped the ground beef and italian sausage.  Also added a little crushed red pepper to spice it just a bit.  Served this for dinner and I personally ate leftovers for breakfast AND lunch the next day.  Made a HUGE vat of sauce using the "almost gallon size" (I call it the industrial size can) of Contadina chopped tomatoes from Sams and added the spices/onions/garlic, etc in proportionate amts.  Cooked in crock pot and served over spaghetti with some sliced fresh Mozzarella cheese over the top - I will NEVER buy sauce to "doctor up" again.  This was the bomb....and I might add my family LOVES italian.  It made about 7 meals with probably enough leftover for 6 more servings....but we like ample amts of sauce.  Takes a little more time than popping open a jar but well worth the effort when you sit down to enjoy it.

text:
Sounded a bit meaty with almost 2 pounds of meat, but went ahead and tried it anyway. The recipe is very similar to my own, with more meat of course,a slight variance in the spices and the addition of fennel and some extra tomato paste. After reading all the rave reviews I had to try it. My husband assured me that there is "nothing wrong with my sauce and no need to try another one." I however, wanted to see what all the fuss was about so I tried it out. I followed the recipe closely but did add a couple of bay leaves,brown sugar instead of white, and sauteed the onion and garlic in olive oil rather than with the meat as I didn't want to lose any of the flavor when I drained the meat. I put it in the crock pot on high for about 3 1/2 hrs then turned to low for about 1 hour. Tasted great! The fennel is a nice addition. The meatieness is perfect for lasagna, however, I would use less if making it to pour over pasta. All in all a great sauce. Thanks John.

text:
This is a great sauce recipe. It's very close to my own homemade sauce minus the fennel (I don't really see it fitting into this recipe, but to each his own!). I try to cook delicious but healthy foods for my family, so I do often add sausage, but only about 1/4 pound and the rest of the meat is lean ground turkey. It's just enough sausage to add a bit of punch, but not ruin the dish nutritionally. I also got a tip from one of the best cooks I've ever known and that is to always add a cap full of whiskey to your pasta sauce (any pasta sauce). (Okay, just for clarification, that is a CAP full, not a cup full! lol) Anyway, I don't know why, but it makes all the difference! It takes the place of the sugar in the sauce. Give it a try and see what you think. (Don't worry, once in the sauce, you can't taste or even smell the whiskey. It just blends into the sauce and somehow makes it exceptional!)

text:
Fabulous home made sauce!  This is the sauce from a similarly named "Word's Best Lasagna" recipe.  The lasagna is pretty good, but the sauce is close to extraordinary by itself.  Great consistency, amazing flavor.  I made the recipe exactly as written.  Next time, I will leave out the fennel and maybe add some parmesan cheese to the sauce.  Fennel is not my favorite spice, and although it wasn't obvious in the sauce, the few times I noticed the flavor of fennel was a little distracting.  The cheese is something that can be added at the end, but I love the zing of mixing it in.  Thanks for the recipe.  Oh, and I would definitely recommend making it the day before and refrigerating overnight to blend flavors.  This is a big batch, so you will have some to freeze.

text:
OMG!  Delicious!  I've made this twice and followed the recipe exactly and loved the result.  And so did my 4 year old.  But like any great recipe, this is not set in stone.  In my 3rd, 4th and 5th versions of this sauce, I've done something different due to what was in my fridge at the time and to whom I was serving.  I cut the sugar but added red wine, or added ground turkey, tried different veggies or added a cheese rind as another reviewer suggested.  While some versions I thought were better than others, all versions were voraciously eaten to those it was served.   I've decided to make a huge batch of this sauce once a month, freeze some and use the rest in another pasta recipe.  Thanks.

text:
I made this last night- I am very picky with my pasta sauce and it was wonderful.  I made only a couple of changes and it came out great... I omitted the water because I find it makes it too watery and I like my sauce a little thicker.  I used crushed tomatoes with basil already in them instead of adding dried and I omitted the fennel because my husband is not a fan.  I also added just a teaspoon of chili powder.  The key really is to let it simmer for a long time- it combines all of the flavors together so well.  Don't make this sauce heat it and serve- it will not be the same it has to simmer!  Loved and will be  my go to meat sauce from now on!

Loved this recipe. I did make changes based on what I had in my pantry so stop reading if you want to know how it turns out if followed exactly! Used 1 28 oz can of petite diced tomatoes (drained the can off), omitted the paste (had none), used 2 tsp of Ital seasoning on accident, used garlic salt in place of regular and equiv of 1 clove of minced garlic, used minced onion from spice rack (1 1/2 T)to save time, omitted ground beef, omitted water, omitted fennel - it is in sausage anyway. Used cream of mushroom soup and threw some frozen peas on the bottom of the casserole (didn't cook them first).  I actually used shredded asiago cheese for a little extra sharpness. This is a great sauce.  While yes, I do some tweaks of my own, it is excellent as written.  My families personal preferences call for hot ground Italian sausage instead of sweet, and we throw in a bag of mini pepperonis as well.  I also double the batch and use 1 28oz can crushed tomatoes and 1 28oz can petite diced tomatoes to add some extra texture. I was really pleased with the way this came out. I would rate it more like 4 1/2 stars based off the fact I tweaked the recipe a little. I used hot breakfast sausage from Jimmy Deans instead of the sweet sausage. I cooked the ground beef and sausage seperate from the sauce due to the grease factor. I also added oregano, a touch of garlic powder, and upped the amount of other spices. I ended up only using 1 can of tomato paste becuase I didn't want the sauce to thick. I let the sauce simmer for 30 minutes then added the meat. Then I let the sauce with the meat simmer for another 1.5 hours.  I loved the addition of the fennel seed also. I will definitely be making this again and will never buy the jar stuff again.

text:
What can I say except it's great? Nice and meaty, full of flavor. I use the bulk ground Johnsonville Italian sausage for recipes like this and like it very much. I don't know if they sell it ground in packages everywhere, but if they do have it, it's right by the ground pork. You can adjust the spices in this to your taste--I add extra fennel, garlic, and I add crushed red pepper. I sub a grated carrot for the sugar (I got that idea from identifying carrots in my favorite pasta sauces from restaurants here--all the ones I like the best have a carrot in them!) Thanks for the recipe -- best sauce I've ever made at home, a great blend of spices, almost nothing left out! Go easy on the salt, by the way -- canned veggies & Italian sausage have some already, plus most of us are going to serve this with canned cheese (you know you have some, and you know it's 99% salt, 1% cheese.) I plan ahead when I'm using that stuff to not oversalt!

text:
I knew better when I looked at the overload of cans of tomato items but since this sauce had so many great reviews, I decided to make it exactly as directed.  This is a pasta sauce for people that like a super heavy, tomato sauce.  I made it to put in my lasagna dish.  For that purpose it works.  You can regulate how much sauce to use and it is very flavorful (if you LOVE tomatoes) and does not take over if you do not use too much.  I ended up giving the leftover sauce to my neighbor that is used to bottled sauces.  He loved it.  Don't waste your money on the sweet sausage.  You can't taste the meat or anything else because of the overload of tomato products.

Bravo John, Bravo! I made this for dinner tonight and cant get over how delicious it is. I did however change a few things: 1) I used sweet sausage but crumbled it up instead of slicing it not a big difference 2) Instead of water I used  cup of strong red wine and  cup of chicken stock. Im glad I make this change because the wine faded nicely into the background of the dish but added depth to it. 3) Instead of ground beef I used high quality frozen meatballs which my family likes. And 4) I used my slow cooker and simmered on low for about 6 hours, allowing all the dried herbs time to season properly. I love this sauce and while I love the convenience of jarred sauces, they all fall short of the flavor of this one. Thank you for a truly great recipeBravo!

This is excellent! I combined suggestions from a bunch of reviewers, added a few touches of my own, and it was a great! Here is what I did:  exclude Italian sausage, and used extra ground beef; add diced peppers (use your favourite colour - I used yellow); replace the water with red wine; I didn't have Italian seasoning, so I used about 1 tsp of oregano, and 1/2 tsp of rosemary, and an extra dash of basil; add red pepper flakes - I used about 1 tsp; make sure you don't put too much fennel because it is really strong

text:
There was something missing from the taste of this sauce and I can't quite put my finger on it, thus the 4 stars.  After cooking for an hour, I took a taste and was surprised that the dominant flavor was simply tomato sauce.  I was expecting a bouquet of Italian spiciness and it just wasn't there.  I added a teaspoon of oregano and this did little to increase the robustness of this sauce.  I'm giving this 4 stars because I'm confident that were I to use some of the tweaking suggested by other raters, this sauce will become amazing.
UPDATE:  I've made this sauce a ton since my initial review.  I've tweaked it by cutting the sugar in half, adding an additional 1/2 tsp of Italian seasoning, 1/2 tsp of fennel, 1/2 tsp of oregano and two bay leaves.  These changes have really kicked up the flavor of the sauce.

LOVE this sauce! It's absolutely amazing and the only sauce recipe I use now. The only slight changes I made were to substitute red wine for the water and brown sugar for the white. I'll usually use turkey sausage instead of pork, but both are delicious. After browning the onions, garlic, and meats, I'll throw everything into a slow cooker and let it cook all day. By dinner time, the house smells wonderful and it tastes like you've spent hours over a hot stove.

country:

text:
I used this recipe as a base and it was wonderful! I altered a few things from the very start, based upon the top positive and negative reviews. I would say it is hands down the best red sauce I've had...and I'm super picky.



I added a 3/4cup onion more...just my preference
Three cloves garlic (preference)
15oz tomato sauce (sweet basil flavor)
Substituted a 1/2cup Sauvignon Cabernet for the water and sugar
No fennel seed (if you're using sweet italian sausage)
Added 1 teaspoon oregano
Lots of salt and pepper. I go by sight and preference! Taste as you go YUMM!



I cooked the sausage (155F), 
ground beef 
and the onion/mushroom/green pepper/garlic mixture*



...in three separate pans. Cook all three completely. 



*Start cooking the onions and mushrooms together first in a pan of medium low olive oil. Add a small chopped green pepper. Add garlic the last two minutes. The whole thing should take about 15min.


Combine both meats and onion/garlic mixture in a large pan. Add the crushed tomatoes, tomato paste, tomato sauce, red wine and seasonings. Bring to simmer and follow above instructions OR


I transferred it all into a 5.5quart Crock Pot and cook on high for 3.5hrs, stirring occasionally. BEST.SAUCE.EVER.


My advice is to add more of what you like/prefer. Happy cooking!!

text:
WOW!  This recipe is truly outstanding!  Yes, you could tweak it but my husband and I absolutely love its flavor as it reminds us of Venice! I did do one thing different.  My husband was a "cattle buyer" throughout his life before retiring, so we have a different perspective on the beef industry.  I substituted ground brisket for the ground beef which my husband grinds and packages himself. The brisket is less per pound than lean hamburger in the market so a little work yields an outstanding product!  We have discovered the small, finer, meat markets use this technique which leaves their clientele raving about their hamburger, and of course they tell their people it's a "special family secrete"! Thank you for sharing this wonderful recipe! By the way, we use a small electric grinder so anyone can do it! -Coastal Sal

Turned out to be very tasty. I didn't have Italian sausage so used only ground beef, although can imagine it would bring up more flavor. Definitely should use wine for water. I didn't have fennel seed but in addition to basil and Italian seasoning I added, as one reviewer suggested, 1/2 tsp of oregano and 2 bay leaves. It's a very nice basic recipe to have with which it's easy to play with as in any way it comes out very flavorful!

Yes, excellent recipe and easy to customize! I made it as is with one modification: I added a dry red wine instead of water because I really felt water would dilute it too much. I also cooked it in a slow cooker (prepared as is, then transferred to a slow cooker for 4 hours).  The taste was very flavorful without being overbearing and perfectly thick. I am not a fan of fennel but the small amount compliments the sausage really well.  
Next time, I will add bay leaves (not sure it "needs" it), mushrooms and try ground turkey as oposed to ground beef.

I made it a few days ago and subbed red wine for the water, brown sugar for the white, and cooked it in the crockpot for 6 hours on low heat. It was wonderful! Be forewarned that this is a very thick and hearty sauce. If you prefer a mild marinara this is not the recipe for you :)

text:
I believe in the importance of advertising accuracy. The title of World's Best Pasta Sauce is a bit of a statement, isn't it?  Sorry, just keeping it real.  Frankly, I think the title should more appropriately be The Best Darn Pasta Sauce You'll Ever Make at Home in the World... Ever...Period!  Seriously, the sauce is delicious and relatively simple.  The most difficult thing is planning your time around the 1 1/2 hours of simmering.  I've followed other recipes that were just as good but were substantially more complicated and more time consuming.  Why do that when you can do this?  This recipe offers a great return on investment (for all you bankers out there).

I discovered this sauce by making it for the original lasagne recipe. This has become my red sauce staple for quite awhile now. Everyone I make it for just LOVES it. I cut back a tad on the sugar and sometimes use spicy sausage instead of sweet ..or if I don't have sausage on hand i'll just use all ground beef.  This recipe is one of my favorites....and so simple to make! Thank you John Chandler!

city:

region:

country:
None
text:
I love this recipe. My whole family does. Sometimes we switch it up with spicy sausage. I also add a tiny bit of red pepper flakes.  Another way I changed this up a bit was by doing the following;  Instead of browning the sausage, beef, onions and garlic all together, I brown them separately. I start with a splash of olive oil and brown the sausage under med-high heat. Once nice and browned I take out the meat and grease and return the pan to the heat. I add a bit of red wine and deglaze the pan. Once all alcohol is boiled out, I reserve for the rest of the liquids. I then clean the pan and do the same w/ the beef. After the beef, I drain the fat and deglaze again. Add the onions and garlic, cooking until translucent. Deglaze again. Then add the spices and all liquids.  Mnnnnn... So good!-

text:
This was a good base recipe for the kind of sauce I was looking for. I made the following changes: used ground turkey and hot turkey italian sausage. I also sauteed some onion, bell pepper and garlic and threw that into the crock pot with all the tomato stuff and seasonings. After that I added some ground turkey that I had slightly cooked with salt, pepper, italian seasoning and red pepper flakes. I also added in the sausage after cooking that and removing the skins (i'm picky about my meat). I let it sit in the crock pot on LOW LOW LOW for about 4 hours until we were ready to eat it. It was reaaaaalllllly good and I will definitely be making again. The BF said it was the best (ok..ok..albeit..only) homemade spaghetti sauce he's ever had :P

While I'm not sure that this is the world's best pasta sauce (that's certainly saying a lot and covering a lot of ground!), I must say that this is a very, very good one!  After about half an hour, I tasted this and it was still a little sweet and acidic for our tastes, so I added a splash of worcestershire sauce, a package of Lipton dry onion soup mix, and probably about 1/2 - 1 tsp. garlic powder.  It was awesome!  This may not be the world's BEST pasta sauce, but it's certainly in the running!

text:
This sauce is great.  I make it all the time now instead of buying it in the jar.  I cook the meat, garlic, and onion (I used fresh onion instead of minced)and then I add it to the rest of the ingredients in the slow cooker.  Set it on low and let it cook all day.  I did change a couple of things though just for personal preference.  Instead of the crused tomatoes, I add a can of Italian Style chopped tomatoes.  I like the chunks of tomatoes and the seasonings in the tomatoes are great.  I also use the bulk sweet italian sausage instead of the links.  This is the greatest sauce I have ever made.  Thanks for a great recipe.

text:
WOW was this good! I omitted the fennel seed bc I hate black licorice and anything that tastes like it. I also added 1/3 cup of red wine & 1 packet of pizza peppers (about 1 tsp red peppers). I probably put too much meat in (I mean, what was I going to do with 1/4 lb of ground beef? I had it pre-packaged in 1 lb packages in my freezer), so I ended up adding another can of tomato sauce to make it less thick. I also used diced tomatoes instead, bc I was making it for spaghetti & thought the whole tomatoes might make it more difficult to eat. 

My friend's kids loved it SO much that they were calling me Miss Chef and saying they wanted to come to my house for dinner more often! This will be made again in my house for sure!!

Spaghetti has been my favorite meal since I was probably 5 years old, so I've tried a lot of sauces over the years, always looking for The One. I found this and made it exactly as suggested except for two things: 
1) I took the onion and pureed it with the tomato sauce because I can't stand any pieces of onion but I like the flavor.  
2) I accidentally used moose breakfast sausage instead of regular ground moose in place of the ground beef! But the sausage was mild enough to where I don't think its a huge difference. I don't eat beef so I will keep substituting it with wild meat or turkey.  
I have to tell you, after 33 years of searching, I am done. This is going to be the go-to spaghetti sauce recipe for me! Thank you so much for sharing.

text:
I followed the recipe mostly. I used sliced stewed tomatoes instead of crushed tomatoes for chunkier texture, and I mashed them some as it cooked. I didnt have any tomato sauce, so I used vegetable broth to thin out the mixture a little. I coarsely chopped the onion, again for a chunkier texture. I didnt pay attention to the portions on seasoning and just seasoned to taste. I used this as a sauce for spaghetti, and ate only a couple of servings. Im a single guy with no kids, this was a lot of sauce to have left over. Fearing that the spaghetti noodles would gum up if refrigerated them separately, I decided to mix the rest of the sauce with the rest of the noodles, topped it off with an Italian cheese blend and baked it for about a half hour. Its been great as leftovers for lunch.

I have been using this site for years to get inspiration on new recipes, but this is the very first review Ive taken the time to write. I first found the Worlds Best Lasagna recipe and it was such a HUGE hit with my family and friends! Naturally, I made this recipe with homemade fettuccini noodles (my Italian in-laws take their Italian food very seriously). Its FANTASTIC! You can make as-is for a wonderful sauce, and over time I have modified a couple of things just based on personal preference. I use brown sugar instead of white, red wine (usually a medium to bold) instead of water, add garlic powder to the meat when Im cooking it, and add a 1/2 tsp each of oregano, rosemary, cinnamon, and nutmeg. John, you are the BEST! Thank you for sharing your recipes.

I cooked a lot for myself when I was single but not much since I married 25 years ago. We have two kids, both of us work and are active. We eat pre-made foods a good deal. This week I decided I wanted to make homemade sauce for Sunday dinner. I found this recipe, read the reviews and off to the store I went. The sauce came out great. I followed the cooking instructions ... very simple. I have a couple non-beef eaters in the house so I substituted ground chicken for the beef and hot Italian turkey sausage (if it can really be called that) for pork. For real meat eaters, this may have been less tasty but for my family it was great. I also only used 1tsp of Fennel. I never cooked with it before so I went easy with it. This is my recipe now for Italian dishes.

THE BEST SAUCE!!!

After calling it quits to jarred pasta sauces, can't find one that doesn't have a weird aftertaste. I was soo happy to stumble across this recipe. My only changes are I use Chicken or Turkey Italian Sausage (the hubby doesn't eat piggy) and no fennel. This sauce is amazing. Love love love this sauce. Thanks for sharing :)

text:
I'm glad to see that he posted just the sauce by itself, not because the lasagna isn't wonderful (we've always gotten rave reviews from all of the people we've made it for), but because I use the extra sauce on my pasta.  As the guy in the house who can't eat cheese, I miss out on the lasagna my family loves, but I can't recommend this sauce enough.  The only thing I add to the pasta afterwards, other than the sauce, is a bit of freshly toasted pinenuts.  You can't go wrong.  The one thing we do do differently is use only ground beef, and simmer it on low in the crockpot for 10-12 hours. Your house will smell amazing!

text:
Ever since I found John's recipe for "World's Best Lasagna" (a must try if you haven't already done so), I've been using the sauce portion of that recipe for my meat sauce. The only minute changes I make for the sauce only are 1) I leave out the fennel seed, and 2) I add a chopped jalapeno, seeds, membranes and all for a little zing. I also give it a quick mix with a submersible blender to puree it a bit. One other change I'd like to note: If you read the lasagna recipe, it doesn't say to drain the meat after browning with the onion and garlic (and jalapeno in my version). I never have drained off the fat and the sauce still never comes out greasy. I just can't see sacrificing the onion, garlic and jap flavors to drain off the fat. If you are going to drain, I would suggest adding the onion and garlic afterward. This really is a fantastic sauce recipe that you absolutely must try. Thank you John!

Made this sauce last night and the family loved it.  As others have suggested, I cooked the sausage and beef (both the lowest fat I could find) together, then removed from the pan and drained on a paper towel.  Cooked the onions and garlic in a little EVOO until wilted then added the tomatoes, sauce, paste and spices.  I did all a 1/4 cup of red wine and about 1/4 cup of water. Let this simmer for about 1/2 hour and added the meat back for the remaining hour. Really liked the fennel.  This one is a keeper!
